    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText16605596710914676699" style="display:none"><i>How do you defy</i> DESTINY?<br /><br />Helen Hamilton has spent her entire sixteen years trying to hide how different she is - no easy task on an island as small and sheltered as Nantucket. And it's getting harder. Nightmares of a desperate desert journey have Helen waking parched, only to find her sheets damaged by dirt and dust. At school she's haunted by hallucinations of three women weeping tears of blood... and when Helen first crosses paths with Lucas Delos, she has no way of knowing they're destined to play the leading roles in a tragedy the Fates insist on repeating throughout history.<br /><br />As Helen unlocks the secrets of her ancestry, she realizes that some myths are more than just legend. But even demigod powers might not be enough to defy the forces that are both drawing her and Lucas together - and trying to tear them apart.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

      That person should run when they see me coming

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer156618864&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156618864" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15844975161852192124">No, GoodReads. <br/><br/>NO.<br/><br/>How about NO FUCKING STARS?<br/><br/>Quick, someone get me chocolate. Lots and lots of chocolate!<br/><br/><a href='http://s181.photobucket.com/albums/x95/shellnick2003/?action=view&current=photo-73.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347446ra/701813.gif' alt='Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I should have known that when Lauren Kate blurbed this book I wouldn't like it. No, wait, that doesn't fully express my hatred for <em>Starcrossed</em>. How about this:<br/><br/>After reading this shit storm of a book I feel like I should go straight to my book shelf and give "Catastrophe": <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664-hush-hush' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hush, Hush</a>,  "My Eyes, They Bleed!": <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30183.Marked' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>House of Night</a>, "Kill it with Fire!": <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twilight</a>, and even, yes,  "Are You Fuckin' </span>
  <span id="freeText15844975161852192124" style="display:none">No, GoodReads. <br><br>NO.<br><br>How about NO FUCKING STARS?<br><br>Quick, someone get me chocolate. Lots and lots of chocolate!<br><br><a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/albums/x95/shellnick2003/?action=view&amp;current=photo-73.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347446ra/701813.gif" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I should have known that when Lauren Kate blurbed this book I wouldn't like it. No, wait, that doesn't fully express my hatred for <em>Starcrossed</em>. How about this:<br><br>After reading this shit storm of a book I feel like I should go straight to my book shelf and give "Catastrophe": <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664-hush-hush" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Hush, Hush</a>,  "My Eyes, They Bleed!": <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30183.Marked" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Night</a>, "Kill it with Fire!": <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>, and even, yes,  "Are You Fuckin' Kidding Me?!": <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10335701-carrier-of-the-mark" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Carrier of the Mark</a> all 5 glorious stars.<br><br>This is the worst book I have ever read.<br><br>Why, oh, why did I read it? I should have listened to the Fates (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105518484" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203089840" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Paige</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158310700" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Phoebe</a>). They warned me of this, but I didn't listen. I almost ALWAYS agree with them on books. Why did I think this would be a different story? I will never doubt your wisdom again, ladies.<br><br>This one time I let myself be influenced by another popular reviewer who claimed to absolutely love this book. I was conned! Fooled! Bamboozled! Hoodwinked!<br><br>The only logical answer is that Hades himself was behind the plot to fry my remaining brain cells. *rubs chin* Yes, that must be it. I've been trolled by the Lord of the Underworld himself.<br><br>HADES!!<br><br>ARE YOU HAPPY?!<br><br>ARE YOU FUCKING HAPPY NOW?!<br><br>WHAT DO YOU HAVE TO SAY FOR YOURSELF?!<br><br><a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/03/20120302-122114.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347446i/701814.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="210" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Y-y-you heartless bastard.<br><br>This review will not be nice. No one will be spared. Not even the children. <br><br> *flips through her notebook*<br><br>Good thing I took <em>plenty</em> of notes then. Hahahaha!<br><br><strong>The Writing</strong><br><br>Dear, Gandhi! It was terrible! Immediately when I started to read, I felt my eye balls start rebuking me. "Noooooooooo, don't make us! You are evil! You are heartless! Why do you hate us! We've been good to you!" I'm not exaggerating when I say this was amateur at best and eye-bleeding bad at worse. The book is littered with ridiculously  simple sentences that remind me of a children's book. "See <s>Helen</s> Spot run? <s>Helen</s> Spot can run fast! Run, <s>Helen</s> Spot. Run!" Metaphors and similes exsit for a reason. Let's use them. But that's not event the worst of it. There were countless pages of info-dumping as well. SHOW DON'T TELL! And the dialogue...OMFG. It was painfully obvious that they were trying entirely too hard to sound like "hip" teens.<br><blockquote>
<em>"What the holy hand grenade was that?"</em><br><br>It felt goofy as hell.<br><br>"Unbefrickinglievable," Hector cusses quietly into the silence.</blockquote><br>I just wanted to shake them. Shake them all.<br><br><strong>The Plot</strong><br><br>The plot was a damn mess. Basic run down:<br><br>- Lucas and his Brady Bunch family move to the neighborhood.<br>- Helen and Lucas almost kill each other.<br>- They break curse/spell/whatever and fall in love over night.<br>- Oh noz! Helen is in danger.<br>- Helen suddenly becomes a sex kitten.<br>- Lucas denies her advances.<br>- Helen wonders if he is gay. Contemplates sex change.<br><blockquote>"...she decided that if Lucas was gay then she was going to have to get a sex change operation. He would be so worth it."</blockquote><br>- Demi-god training.<br>- Oh, but wait! Now, she is invincible!<br>- "Sex, please," says Helen. "No means no, Helen. It would destroy the world!" Lucas cries.<br>- Shit happens, people die.<br>- "OMG! So we won't destroy the world after all! I'm horny. Let's do it," Lucas declares. *rams tongue down throat* "Ew. We are first cousins! We can never be together! Fuck our fuckin' life!" she whines.<br><br>Fin.<br><br><a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/03/photo-198.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347446i/701815.jpg" alt="" width="279" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><em>Keep up Hades! </em><br><br>Angelini tries to confuse the readers with her many plot twists, but all the plot really does is run around the mulberry bush chasing the weasel. There was nothing clever about it. I could tell that I was supposed to be like, "Whoa! My teeny little brain never saw that coming!" <em>IT NEVER HAPPENED! </em><br><br><strong>Helen</strong><br><br>Let's play <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/MarySue" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Name That Sue</a>! But first you're going to need a few clues about her personality:<br><br>- I'm super beautiful, but I don't notice it!<br>- I'm the "last" person in my family. Woe is me!<br>- I'm so powerful <em>and</em> useless, love me!<br>- I'm so selfless. Here, let me love you!<br>- My characterization has been used over and over in tons of books, but I have super <em>speshul</em> powers!  I'm kewler than them!<br>Answers: <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/BlackHoleSue" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Hole Sue</a>, <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/GodModeSue" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">God Mode Sue</a>, <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/SympatheticSue" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Sympathetic Sue</a>, <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/AntiSue" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Anti-Sue</a>... my god. It's too many Sues to count! It's a <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/ThirtySuePileup" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Thirty Sue Pileup</a>!<br><br>Helen is an idiot.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347446ra/701816.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Most of the novel she's running around with twinkling stars in her eyes and clueless to everything that is happening around her. She is beautiful in every way. So much so, that it is normal for people to just sit and stare at her. Everybody loves her and the world kisses her ass every chance it gets. Her favorite hobbies include going grocery shopping, cooking for her dad, doing homework, and personal hygiene. Oh hey, Bella! I didn't see you there!<br><br>The moment Helen and Lucas stop attempting to end each other's life, they immediately start holding hands and declaring their love for one another. (Oh, insta-love! How I hate thee!) She's never had a boyfriend or been kissed until Lucas and his family move into town. There is just something about Lucas that brings out everything in Helen. And I do mean everything. Her entire life she has had all these powerful mystical powers, but she never knew about them because whenever she would use them unknowingly in front of mortals she would get a nasty bout of menstrual cramps! Little does Helen know that her cramps were a cursed placed on her by her very own mother. But it was totally for her protection. Of course. *eyeroll* If that isn't some bullshit, I don't know what is.<br><br>So anyway, with every new plot twist, Helen seems to get a new power. Which basically means she keeps getting more and more useless. All she does is say, "Oh, but I don't want to hurt anyone! Even if they are trying to kill me, I can't justify their deaths!" Are you kidding me? She has no sense of self-preservation.<br><br><blockquote>"I knew if I started blocking him he'd just get angrier, and then I would eventually have no choice by to hit him so hard he wouldn't be able to hit me back."</blockquote><br>She.is.a.<strong>demi-god</strong>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347446ra/701817.gif" alt="" width="400" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <em>Go on and let it out, Hades!</em><br><br>That was during a SELF-DEFENSE session. How is it that a character can be so powerful and do NOTHING with her powers? What is the point?!*breath in, breath out* Sorry, guys. The stupidity makes it hard to breath. Thankfully, one of the other characters noticed this madness and said:<br><br><blockquote>"She'd better get it in her. Because I don't want any of the people I love to die defending her lazy ass."<br>
</blockquote><br>That was the only good part of the entire book. &gt;_&gt;<br><br>Then I hit the next chapter and Cassandra has a sword aimed for Helen's head and she JUST STANDS THERE.<br><br><blockquote>Cassandra swung her sword. In that millisecond Helen knew she'd had a good life, because she suddenly loved it so much that she could have wept with gratitude. She'd had amazing friends, the best dad in the world, and a strong, healthy body...<br>
</blockquote>I thought she was going to finally die! I was like, "Yes! KILL HER NOW! Doooo iiiittttt!" And you know what happens? She levels up out of nowhere!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347446i/701818.png" alt="" width="360" height="252" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><em>Why won't she roll over and die already?!</em><br><br>So now she's invincible and can't be killed by any weapons <em>AND</em> she's the most powerful demi-god. REALLY?! &gt;Implied Facepalm&lt;<br><br>Yet, believe it or not all those things I could have semi-forgiven and gave this book 1 star, maybe 2 for good effort. The biggest problem with this book: <strong>It's SEXIST. </strong>This book offended me on so many levels, it's not even funny. Let me count the ways:<br><br><strong>Causal jokes about domestic abuse:</strong><br><br><em>"I'll just tell him you abuse me," she said with a shrug. "And I'll tell him you like it," he teased back.</em><br>That shit is not amusing. AT ALL. Lots of women suffer from domestic abuse every day and Angelini pokes fun?! What messages are we sending our young girls? That this is romantic banter? This is why young girls think it is okay to tweet crazy shit like they would let Chris Brown hit them any time. This is why we are seeing people happy about him singing songs with Rihanna. We need to speak up against this. IT IS NOT OKAY!  OMG, I'm so angry right now, I'm seeing red. <strong>RAGE.</strong><br><br><strong>Use your powers in the kitchen!:</strong><br><blockquote>Everything about <strong>Ariadne was so feminine and round and lovely</strong> that Helen simply couldn't imagine anyone hitting her. "Do you guys do this to each other often? The fighting, I mean." Ariadne was shaking her head before Helen had even finished talking. "No. We spar together <strong>to stay in shape</strong>, but <strong>only the boys really fight</strong>, and only when they need to get something off their chests."</blockquote><br>WHAT?!  The only reason why they fight is to <em>stay in shape</em>? THEY ARE DEMI-GODS!!!!!<br><br><strong>Controlling boyfriend:</strong><br><blockquote>"Now go to sleep," <strong>he ordered.</strong><br>
</blockquote><br>Come again? He what?! Oh,<em> hell</em> no. Let a guy come home and start ordering me around. I've got two words for him:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347446ra/701819.gif" alt="" width="400" height="216" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <em>Bitch, please.</em><br><br><blockquote>He kissed her neck and said he was sorry over and over, but try as she might, he wouldn't let her face him. <strong>She began to feel like she was being used.</strong><br>
</blockquote><br>OMGOMGOMGOMGOMGOMG.<br><br><blockquote>"Is Zach after you?" Lucas asked with wide eyes.<br>"Oh, not really. He wants to talk to me about something, I think," Helen said as if it wasn't important. She shut her mouth before she could say too much.<br>"Yeah, I'll bet," Lucas said with a sneer, his blue eyes turning nearly black as he sensed her untruth. Is there any reason for Zach to think that you might be single?"<br>
</blockquote><br>At this point he never even asked her to be his girl friend! He goes throughout most of the book just holding her hand, but telling everyone else they don't really have a relationship. And then he pulls this line:<br><blockquote>"Are you trying to make me jealous or are you just so frustrated that you're already looking for someone else? Someone who would give in to you?"<br>
</blockquote><br>I just... can't.<br><br><strong>Women should be held to high standards and oh, yeah, they're evil:</strong><br><blockquote>"<em>A lady never cheapened herself by using foul language."</em><br>
</blockquote><br>And:<br><blockquote>
  <em>"He had sworn to remove the <strong>feminine evil</strong> of the cestus from the world so that <strong>all men could control their lust.</strong></em>
</blockquote><br>Yup, thats right. It's totally a woman's fault a man can't control himself. I can't believe women have been fighting for RIGHTS just so we can write about this kind of stuff! Around 80% this book gets super ridiculous with making Helen and her mother out to be "semxy sex pots". Helen is so damn <s>useless</s> powerful and horny that she pretty much starts playing Lady GaGa's <em>Love Game, </em>trying to take off Lucas' clothes at every opportunity she gets.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347446ra/701820.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><em>Let's have some fun this beat is sick. I wanna take a ride on your disco stick!</em><br><br>I suppose this is what she is supposed to look like:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347446i/701821.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><em>I can see you staring there from across the block with a smile on your mouth and a hand on your HUH!</em><br><br>There are a ton of other problems with this book, but I've wasted enough of my life with Starcrossed. I probably have enough anger and quotes to write a damn book myself. I just... can't. I'm offended this was written. I offended that it was published. I offended people think this is okay.<br><br>This book FAILED at failing.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347446i/701822._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="365" height="223" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>More reviews and other cool things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15844975161852192124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105518484?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-rants">kat-s-rants</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=just-plain-bad">just-plain-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=ya-pnr-maddness">ya-pnr-maddness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer105518484&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105518484" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12783379905344116986">Starcrossed is the story of a teenage school girl, Helen, who meets new boy, Lucas, and tries to murder him with her bare hands for no reason. Lucas, also, wishes to kill Helen in a horrifically violent way because they’re both demigods on the opposite side of a war.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335625i/694448.png' alt='corny romantic picture' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I really thought this book was going to kill me – either with hypertension or an aneurysm for all the times it had me almost screaming in frustration. For example:<br/><br/>Lucas is violently dragging Helen out of a supermarket. Helen doesn’t </span>
  <span id="freeText12783379905344116986" style="display:none">Starcrossed is the story of a teenage school girl, Helen, who meets new boy, Lucas, and tries to murder him with her bare hands for no reason. Lucas, also, wishes to kill Helen in a horrifically violent way because they’re both demigods on the opposite side of a war.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335625i/694448.png" alt="corny romantic picture" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really thought this book was going to kill me – either with hypertension or an aneurysm for all the times it had me almost screaming in frustration. For example:<br><br>Lucas is violently dragging Helen out of a supermarket. Helen doesn’t want to leave and is worried that Lucas is going to kill her but can’t say or do anything or she’ll make a scene.<br><br>No. Fuck no. Girls, if someone is manhandling you against your will then that is actually the <i>perfect</i> time to make a scene! Why is this concept of meek submissiveness in women perpetuated? It literally costs women their lives to be like this. I’m not shitting you. Making a scene saved my life once. Big time. It was the difference between seeing my parents that night – or never again. <br><br>Or what about the part where Helen is debating meeting up with Lucas, who she knows has been trying to hurt her? However, she has a feeling that he won’t kill her because he doesn’t <b>seem like the type.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335625i/694449._SY540_.jpg" alt="Emma Watson looking disgusted" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Are we <i>trying</i> to perpetuate a mindset in young women that could <a href="http://www.rainn.org/get-information/statistics/sexual-assault-offenders" rel="nofollow noopener">directly cause them severe harm?</a><br><br><br>Approximately 2/3 of rapes were committed by someone known to the victim.<br>73% of sexual assaults were perpetrated by a non-stranger.<br>38% of rapists are a friend or acquaintance.<br>28% are an intimate.<br>7% are a relative.<br><br>"Girls ages 16-19 are 4 times more likely than the general population to be victims of rape, attempted rape, or sexual assault."<br><br>Nobody is more vulnerable than the young girls reading these novels yet, consistently, there are messages that impede them from knowing what the right and normal responses are to sexual assault or physical violence perpetuated against them.<br><br>What I also find quite aggravating is that, in this novel, all the girls at school are jealous of Helen because she’s just too beautiful. Look, there are a variety of reasons why people might not like you. Your manners, social skills, lifestyle, personality, politics, religion, race, style, if you like Nickelback…<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335625i/694450.jpg" alt="Nickelback rejected" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you think the only reason that people don’t like you is because you’re just too beautiful then maybe you should reconsider. It’s more likely that they despise you because your head is so far up your own ass that you could perform a colonoscopy with your own nose. And, yes, you’re all welcome for that little mental image.<br><br>But even if you took all these factors away, I STILL wouldn’t like this book. Angelini seems confused over what makes love powerful, or Starcrossed love tragic. Look, it wasn’t just that Romeo and Juliet *spoiler* died that made the story powerful. Lucas and Helen don’t really hate each other and nobody in this story actually has a reason to hate anyone else. It’s all a manufactured emotion by the furies to get them to fight. But this misses the point completely because if the hate isn’t real and thus meaningless, then the love isn’t real and thus meaningless too! Neither are real emotions and both are just created by the furies to perpetuate their story arcs. <br><br>And Lucas and Helen not being together isn’t tragic because they never sacrificed anything to be together anyway. Romeo turned his back on his family and tried to befriend a hated foe, in the process losing his best friend. The tragedy is that he makes a terrible decision and then fate, from that point on, makes it impossible for him to redeem the situation. The tragedy is that Juliet takes a leap of faith, trusts in others and Romeo, is brave enough to step out and defy her family, only to be betrayed by destiny and left to wake alone and deserted in a tomb.<br> <br>My frustration with YA authors is that I think they forget what it’s like to be teenagers and in love. I think they write characters and try to convince the reader that the love these people are experiencing is so strong it can conquer anything – that it’s epic love.<br>Most of the time I don’t think these couples would last a year, let alone eternity. Because, after all, when they survive the scheming madman or the ancient prophecy against their love, will they be able to survive each other? <br><br>The miserly old crone in me thinks, no.<br><br><br>********************************Spoilers below**************************************<br>WTF is up with the ending?! <br><br>Helen: Oh Lucas, I love you so much!<br>Lucas: Helen, I love you too! Our love in unconquerable! Eternal! All-consuming!<br>Helen: Damn the fact that us being together means the gods will unleash their wrath upon the earth and that innocent people will die! Let’s be together anyway!<br>Lucas: I agree! The feelings I have for you are so strong that I can’t stay away – no matter the damage this will do to countless people and to my entire family!<br>Helen: Wait! I just found out that we’re cousins!<br>Lucas: Oh! Gross! Well, I guess I’ll see you around some time then.<br>Helen: Yeah! That was close! Well, have a nice life then, Lucas.<br><br>*Kat tears hair out in frustration* Okay, so possibility of war and danger and impossible obstacles, they can overcome, but the fact that their love impinges on antiquated social norms destroys it? Look, I’m not exactly advocating that you seek out your cousins for the purposes of reproduction here. However, if you were to find out tomorrow that your significant other has been your cousin all along, is it really that big a deal? After all, it is not uncommon for siblings, separated at birth, to accidentally find each other as adults and marry. There’s been more than one case of people finding out after marriage that they were closely related. <br> <br>Also, that they are being separated merely because of the fact that apparently NOBODY can do some basic mathematics?<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><i>Numbers…too… hard…to…subtract!</i><br><br>Lastly, apparently if the furies don’t repeat these storylines, the fabric of the universe is going to come apart. Why...? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335625i/694452.jpg" alt="Tommy Lee Jones being Tommy Lee Jones" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12783379905344116986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_151090769" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151090769" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151090769?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-liked">books-i-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-ought-to-hate-but-don-t">books-i-ought-to-hate-but-don-t</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151090769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5028552527315246621">**EDIT: I originally gave this book three stars, simply because it is based on Greek mythology, and I've had a love affair with Greek mythology since I was a kid. However, upon further consideration and a sudden recall of my Homer and Bullfinch, I am forced to concede that the Greek Mythology in this book is about as authentic as cranberry sauce in a can. So, only two stars, and I'm STILL being generous!<br/><br/><br/><i>Two Twifans are walking down the street to the cinema</i><br/><br/><b>Fangirl 1:</b> ZOMG, I h8 steffie meyer! Y h</span>
  <span id="freeText5028552527315246621" style="display:none">**EDIT: I originally gave this book three stars, simply because it is based on Greek mythology, and I've had a love affair with Greek mythology since I was a kid. However, upon further consideration and a sudden recall of my Homer and Bullfinch, I am forced to concede that the Greek Mythology in this book is about as authentic as cranberry sauce in a can. So, only two stars, and I'm STILL being generous!<br><br><br><i>Two Twifans are walking down the street to the cinema</i><br><br><b>Fangirl 1:</b> ZOMG, I h8 steffie meyer! Y hasn’t she written more Twilight buks alredy? I miss edwrd, n bella is so cool, zomg, I jus cnt get enuf of her!<br><br><b>Fangirl 2:</b> Did u see the trailer fr breaking dawn? Omigod, arnt Robsten the cutest couple eva? I cnt blive we hav 2 w8 til nvmbr fr prt 1! <br><br><b>Fangirl 1:</b> But at least thr r 2 more movies to luk frwrd 2! Wht if smeyer neva writs anuther Twilight buk?! Aftr the movies, wll have nuthin 2 luk forwrd 2! *sobs*<br><br><i>Fangirl 2 spots a poster at the cinema and jumps for joy</i><br><br><b>Fangirl 1:</b> wht r u so excited abt?<br><br>Fangirl 2: <i>
  <b>this</b>
</i>:<br><br><a href="http://s1201.photobucket.com/albums/bb349/vinaya18/?action=view&amp;current=RobstenStarcrossed.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346284i/700713.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Fangirl 1:</b> ZOMG, s thr a new twilight muvi? Y didn’t I know abt this?<br><br><b>Fangirl 2:</b> No silly, it’s tht nu buk by Josephine Angelini, cald Starcrossed. It’s JUST lyk Twilight, bt 4 smarter ppl. Lyk us! It’s so cool, its abt this couple of teenagers who fall in luv, but they cn NEVA B 2GETHR! I hurd dey signed Robsten 4 dis muvi b4 the buk was even printed!<br><br><b>Fangirl 1:</b> *gasps* NO! Did u read de buk? I wnt it NOW! Lts go buy it. And oh! I gotta tell my Tweet peeps abt dis! And put it up on fb! And my space! Oh I cnt w8 2 read dis!<br><br>...and that is why, ladies and gentlemen, Josephine Angelini will be laughing her way to the bank in a couple of months, when the book comes out!<br><br><br>I think I would have enjoyed this book more if the soundtrack of Bella’s Lullaby hadn’t been running in my head the whole time. What is Starcrossed about, you ask. Starcrossed is the story of a painfully shy, socially inept girl who meets a really hot boy with whom she feels an instant ‘connection’ even though they must stay away from each other for fear that one of them may kill the other. However, this (seemingly insurmountable) problem is soon solved when girl and boy save each other’s lives, thereby easing the path to true luurve. The boy has a large, close-knit family, some of whom are warm and welcoming while the others are hostile and suspicious of the girl. The girl, unbeknownst to her, has been super-speshul all her life, but neither this, not her stunning beauty (of which she is also largely unaware) has catapulted her to fame and popularity. In short, she is a wallflower who likes to hide behind her hair. (I wonder if her hair, too, smells of strawberry shampoo? *random Twilight factoid*)<br><br>Anyway, moving on, boy and girl do, of course, fall in love, but they can NEVER be together! Or at least, not without causing the destruction of all human civilisation! (Wow, I knew teenage dating was a minefield, but this is the first time I’ve heard of it being a nuclear warhead!) Of course, boy’s family are very different from the rest of their kind, they don’t believe in killing, except in self-defense, and have moved into a small town to avoid the rest of their clan, who are rabid, psychotic killers. Blessed with extraordinary good looks and great athleticism, the boys of the family are all star footballers.<br><br>Where there is true love, of course, there must be danger. There are a whole bunch of people out to get the girl, including a very dangerous member of boy’s psychopathic extended family. So while girl is busy debating whether boy likes her, since he is making no moves towards her, boy’s cousin is hunting down girl. Girl is being protected by stalker-ish members of boy’s family. Until girl finds out that boy has vowed never to touch her, goes off in a snit, gets attacked, gets rescued, sneaks boy upto her room while oblivious single father watches TV and declares her love, only to find out the shattering truth that keeps them apart. <br><br>Sounding familiar yet?<br><br>Yeah, so basically, this is fanfic. This is what you get when a Twifan decides, why don’t I make Bella and Edward demigods instead of vampires? Why don’t I flip it a little and see what happens if it’s Bella who has the bloodlust and the super-powers right from the beginning? And while I am at it, why don’t I sell my fanfic to a publisher for a million dollars or so? After all, there are over 15 million people worldwide jonesing for a Twilight fix, so I might as well cash in while Smeyer is busy writing about An Alien Called Wanda. <br>But here’s the deal; this is not a badly written book. I would rate it slightly higher on technique than Twilight. And there are parts where the book gets positively interesting, before she ruins it altogether, but more on that later. <br><br>Five reasons why Starcrossed is better than Twilight:<br> 1. The love interest is a teenager the same age as the heroine. No immortal hundred-year old with an inexplicable penchant for cradle-snatching here!<br> 2. Nobody falls in love with their food.<br> 3. No love triangle (thus far!)<br> 4. Greek mythology!!! (even fake Greek mythology is better than fake vampire lore)<br> 5. Claire, the heroine’s best friend, is an actual character, as opposed to a cardboard cutout like whatsherface Angela. (Although the constant references to her height and her fierceness and her hurriedly put-together chemistry with Jason were sort of boring.)<br><br>Unfortunately, the unmistakable resemblance to Twilight sort of killed every other thought in my brain for the duration of this book. It’s not just that the larger plot structure reminded me of Twilight; it’s also very many, many small details. Like Helen’s habit of hiding behind her hair. Like Helen’s brand of awkward, insecure social interaction. Like how she logs on and Googles all the suspicious paranormal people stalking her. Like the fact that Helen’s dad is a single father who spends most of the book watching sports on TV and being away on work at all the crucial times. Like the fact that Helen is so modest she can’t change in front of another girl. Like the fact that Lucas has a loving, close-knit family with a sister who is a seer and can see the future. Like the fact that there is a scene with a car crash from which Lucas emerges unscathed. Like the fact that Lucas manages to sneak into her bedroom without her father knowing, and <i>lies on top of the bedcovers</i> while she lies under them; in fact there is one scene where she brushes her teeth in the bathroom and gets ready quickly for bed while Lucas is waiting for her in the bedroom, then goes to the head of the stairs and yells goodnight to her father, who is watching sport on TV. My memory may be at fault, but isn’t there the <b>EXACT. SAME. SCENE</b> in Twilight? <br><br>Also there are several points in the book where Angelini seems to be trying too hard to refute the fact that she is writing Twilight fanfic. There are references to stalker-ish men, and women who do what they’re told because their men wanted them to, and both characters claim that they don’t indulge in such behaviour. Helen’s best friend is all like, oh you have superpowers, you must be a vampire. And then there are corny vampire jokes. The lady doth protest too much, methinks. <br><br>The only thing this book has in common with the Percy Jackson series is that they are both vaguely based on Greek mythology. And Angelini twists the myths beyond recognition in an attempt to make them fit the parameters of the story. A simple Wiki search would tell her that Helen had no dealings with Aphrodite. And that Paris was the one caught in Aphrodite's clutches. Not to mention the fact Helen is directly descended from Zeus, owing nothing of her conception to Aphrodite. I'm not saying, read the Iliad, but at least read Wikipedia!! And all of her demi-gods are so super, super, SUPER speshul, with a vast array of supernatural knuckle dusters, that even the gods would have difficulty surpassing them! Wish fulfillment much?<br><br>So anyway, I’m breezing along, trying to get Robsten’s faces out of my head, feeling my usual illicit thrill at the idea of star-crossed lovers, when I get to a point in the book that’s actually sort of thrilling, and doesn’t remind me of any other work of fiction. I start to think that maybe there’s some hope for Angelini, after all. And then what does she do? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She channels Cassandra Clare! Yes, Cassandra Clare! A fanfic tribute to the queen of fanfic? Aaaargh! Thankfully, she doesn’t leave us, the readers, in suspense for long, even if her characters are going to be tortured for the next two books, at least! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> As if it’s not enough that Zeus, the Furies and the Fates are conspiring to keep these two desperate lovers apart, she decided she needed to toss the kitchen sink at them as well! <br><br>So why two stars? One star for the fact that the book is written moderately well and paces itself decently; one star for the fact that I get an illicit thrill out of the we-can-never-be-together, no-we-WILL-be-together-against-all-the-odds, i-will-mope-and-only-be-an-empty-shell-if-you-abandon-me plotline, despite the sneers from my saner, feminist alter ego! <br><br>So if you hate Twilight and Twilight fanfic, or you know, badly-researched literature, stay away from this book. If you’re a Twifan desperate for another dose, rush to the stores and pre-book your copy now! If you’re like me and couldn’t care less either way, well, we can band together and nitpick!<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5028552527315246621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Haleema" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema"><img alt="Haleema" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402430795p2/4336293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181650579?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haleema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haleema" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema">Haleema</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=just-begging-for-snark">just-begging-for-snark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=stupid">stupid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=half-wit-characters">half-wit-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=bad-writing">bad-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=not-again">not-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=cheese">cheese</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=hate">hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=pretentious">pretentious</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181650579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13003317757871704473">Beware of spoilers!<br/><br/><b>Characters:</b><br/>So this is where I went <s>slightly</s> balistic. I'm going to talk about the two main freaks of the book.<br/><br/>Helen Hamilton:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380352522ra/705970.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Grams is a Mary Sue. She's so damn perfect and untouchable that it's difficult for me to relate to her. Tall, beautiful, graceful, heavenly. Hence, her nickname, "Heaven Hamilton." Really? She's quite pathetic really. She whines a lot and can't stand if someone makes fun of her, which reminds me of mostly ever other YA MC. She is also very selfish. Espec</span>
  <span id="freeText13003317757871704473" style="display:none">Beware of spoilers!<br><br><b>Characters:</b><br>So this is where I went <s>slightly</s> balistic. I'm going to talk about the two main freaks of the book.<br><br>Helen Hamilton:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380352522ra/705970.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Grams is a Mary Sue. She's so damn perfect and untouchable that it's difficult for me to relate to her. Tall, beautiful, graceful, heavenly. Hence, her nickname, "Heaven Hamilton." Really? She's quite pathetic really. She whines a lot and can't stand if someone makes fun of her, which reminds me of mostly ever other YA MC. She is also very selfish. Especially with her father! Everytime Jerry tries to talk to her or ask her anything, she completely disregards him and flees.<br><br><u>Lucas:</u><br><br>Did he even exist in the book? Lucas makes Edward Cullen look like the most complex character in the world. Lucas was a blank sheet of paper. Without even the college-ruled lines. Oh, yes. However, he did everything he could to make him look like the creepiest man in the world. <br><br>1. He stares at Helen. Typical of a creepy main hero. <br>2. He follows her around. To her house. The market. Anywhere. You name it, he's been there!<br>3. He tells other people to follow her around.<br>4. He tries to kill her, lmao. <br><br>But it's just so romantic, though. Right?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380738150i/3117374._SX540_.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Plot:</u><br>Silly and dull. <br><br><u>Writing:</u><br>Angelini's writing wasn't even there. Where was it? The sentences were simple and short. Imagery was a whole different concept to Angelini. Similes and metaphors? What are they?! And every once in a while, she would bring up a vague word that had nothing to do with the sentences at all. She didn't even seem like she knew what she was talking about.<br><br>I do not know what happens in the next 200 and something pages I decided to not read. I don't even want to know.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_160396726" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160396726" />
    <a title="Cait" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5254851-cait"><img alt="Cait" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320186575p2/5254851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160396726?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cait" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cait" href="/user/show/5254851-cait">Cait</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5254851-cait?shelf=annoying-ending">annoying-ending</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer160396726&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160396726" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10197872199866497597">Alright, I know that I originally rated this book 2.5 stars and, back then, I honestly thought that it deserved that much; I really did. However, a little over a month ago I was given an assignment for my AP class (we were reading the Iliad at the time) to cover the "apology of Helen" as was told in the Odyssey and really her whole life; especially the time when she was in Paris and how she effected the Trojan war. At first I was kind of moaning about it (my GR friends can attest to that) but, t</span>
  <span id="freeText10197872199866497597" style="display:none">Alright, I know that I originally rated this book 2.5 stars and, back then, I honestly thought that it deserved that much; I really did. However, a little over a month ago I was given an assignment for my AP class (we were reading the Iliad at the time) to cover the "apology of Helen" as was told in the Odyssey and really her whole life; especially the time when she was in Paris and how she effected the Trojan war. At first I was kind of moaning about it (my GR friends can attest to that) but, then, as I got more and more into the topic and <i> really </i> finding out as much as I could in that time about Helen. Now, I am far from an expert in the subject; there are still so many opinions that I don't know about (but would really like to) but since I consider myself more well-versed than your average GR member, I will spend this <i> whole </i> review talking about how horribly wrong Angelini is about Helen and Paris' relationship. <br><br><span>[image error]</span><br>Seriously, peeps, this is a <i> lot </i> of research that I am going to include to enlighten you all. <br><br><b> 1. How Angelini suggests that Helen and Paris, "ran off together" and abandoned both Trojans and Greeks like it was something incredibly romantic. </b><br><br>First thing I'm going to address is that THEY DIDN'T FUCKING RUN AWAY ROMANTICALLY! As a little backstory to why Paris even found Helen in the first place was, one day, the three main goddesses (Aphrodite, Hera, and Athena) appeared to Paris while he was tending his sheep, for he was thought to be the most beautiful man in the world (and also the son of king Priam although he didn't know that yet) and asked him to tell them who was the most beautiful. Hera offered him power over many countries, Athena offered him wealth, and Aphrodite promised him the most beautiful woman in existence. Paris, being the <i> exceptional </i> man whore that he his, said Aphrodite was the most beautiful, and she promised him the then Helen of Sparta, then married to Menelaus and already with one child, Hermione. So, one month while Menelaus was out journeying, Paris came and took Helen, with help from Aphrodite. So, backstory over, one of the main ideas held by many artists like Primaticcio and scholars, both ancient and more recent is that Helen <i> was fucking raped as she was taken away by Paris.</i> Then an even bigger majority believe that if she did love Paris, it was because Aphrodite was controlling her emotions making her feel that way (she is the goddess of passion, after all). Some even say that Hera, being so miffed at Paris for not choosing her, sent Helen to live in Egypt for the duration of the war and gave Paris a fake Helen made out of clouds, just to provoke the whole war. One ancient philosopher, Sophocles, actually went so far as to go to Egypt and ask random Egyptians if Helen had been there, and they said yes, although that idea is one of the less well-known ones. Not very.....romantic, now is it? And even if Helen chose to go with him, they didn't "run away" and leave both of their peoples all romantically and such. They ran their asses back to big daddy Priam and let him protect them from the Acheans (also known as the Greeks) when they came to take back what was rightfully theirs. <br><br><span>[image error]</span><br>The art doesn't lie, folks. Oh, and the random nude woman is Aphrodite, making Helen go with Paris.<br><br><b> 2. That female descendants of the half-bloods from the time of the Trojan war on are also super powerful, and that both sexes can fly and have spur speshul powers. </b><br><br>That is, again, <i> a bunch of shit. </i> Not even the <i> males </i> had superpowers all of the time; they only were able to do mind-boggling feats when they were in the aristea (which, in a roundabout way means a scene of glory/ victory) where they put on some shiny armor, fight for a while, get injured, then the gods heal them and <i> grant them strength </i> then they kill an important enemy. They could not fly, they could not control the weather or anything of the sort, the half-blood men were just warriors. Especially the women back in Greek times; any woman who was born of a woman and a god was not even strong. She was just beautiful and that's about it. I know part of why that is is because of the sexist opinions back then, but that's the way it was written and told and that's the way I <i> and </i> Angelini have to and should take it. The only semi-important thing a woman <i> could </i> do back then was be an Oracle or be a priestess to a god/goddess. They were basically only seen as property for men; especially the beautiful ones like Helen. Nowhere in all of my research have I seen a woman or man who has been able to fly or control the weather; maybe if Angelini had laid it out better and used some <i> actual </i> facts then I could have accepted it, but she most obviously didn't, so I'm calling a major amount of bullshit on the whole idea. <br><br><b> 3. That Helen and Paris had a "great love" and loved each other sooooooooooo much. </b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br>Can ya detect the sarcasm?<br><br>This is going to be the longest part of my <s> rant </s> review because this is the <i> biggest </i> most <i> annoying </i> statement that has ever been laid upon my ears. As I said earlier it is a widely known and accepted fact that Helen was forced by both Aphrodite and Paris to leave Menelaus and her daughter. Don't believe me? Here's a quote from the Helen herself as she talks about when the Greeks finally defeated Troy from The Odyssey, a thousand of years-old novel that is considered, along with The Iliad, one of the most important works of literature in early european history:<br><br><i> The rest of the Trojan women shrilled their grief. Not I: / my heart leapt up--my heart had changed by now--I yearned / to sail back home again! I grieved too late for the madness / Aphrodite sent me, luring me there, far from my dear land, / forsaking my own child, my bridal bed, my husband too, / a man who lacked for neither brains nor beauty </i><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br>Notice how there's always a naked woman flying around in the background? It was <i> Aphrodite, </i> peeps.<br><br><i> Still </i> think that she may still like him? Well, here's a scene from The Iliad where she has even more <i> wonderful </i> things to say about Paris; this is where Aphrodite is trying to make Helen come have sex with Paris after he chickened out and left in the middle of a fight between Menelaus and himself:<br><br><i> But why now?-<br>because Menelaus has beaten your handsome Paris<br>and hateful as I am, he longs to take me home?<br>Is that why you beckon here beside me now<br>with all the immortal cunning in your heart?<br>Well, go to him yourself- you hover beside him!<br>Abandon the gods' high road and be a mortal!<br>Never set foot again on Mount Olympus, never!-<br>Suffer for Paris, protect Paris, for eternity...<br>until he makes you his wedded wife- that or his slave.<br>Not I, I'll never go back again!” </i><br><br>Oh, and did I also fail to mention that Helen, when she does go to do it with Paris, and only because Aphrodite forces her, she outright says she wished that he had died on the battlefield? <br><br><s> Do your damned research, Angelini </s><br><br>Honestly, I don't blame the woman; Paris is just about the biggest douchebag in existence (at least that's one thing Angelini got right about Lucas' character). Before he had even taken Helen to be his wife he was about as close that you could be to love back in those days with a concubine named Oenone. On the day that Paris leaves to take Helen on his little secret mission, she comes to the docks and begins to cry in earnest and tells him that if he's injured, she will heal him. Let me tell you that kind of declaration was a big deal back in those days, and what does Paris do? As soon as he has Helen in his greedy little paws he basically "dumps" Oenone. In another scene in the Iliad, when Helen comes up to beg him to at least go <i> fight </i> the Greeks, he's sitting in a room with about ten other concubines, doing who the hell knows what with all of them. When he finds out that Helen had been having sex with one of his sons ( a lot of concubines= a lot of kids) he gets so enraged and jealous that he <i> kills his own son. </i> He has always been a coward as I have shown; he's the one that came up with the quote "I'm a lover not a fighter". But it comes to a point hat he would rather fight the most dangerous human on the planet at that time, Achilles, than be with Helen. Even when he's on his death bed, he doesn't allow Helen to choose her own husband and forces her to marry a man named Deiophobus. <br><br>Yeah.....he sounds like such a <s> controlling bastard </s> loving fellow.....<br><br>The closest that you will get to true love in almost any Greek fable is the story of Hector his wife Andromache, and their son Astyanax (which is kind of ironic because the Iliad was supposed to be all about the glory of the Greeks, but Homer makes us as readers sympathize a lot more with the Trojans than the Greeks). Andromache truly cares about her husband and child, and when he comes to check on them she begs him to not fight and stay with her and their son. Hector replies that he's only fighting because he doesn't want her to be sold into slavery; that's how much he values her has a person, and when he dies Andromache grieves horribly. She describes Hector's death as her own:<br><br><i> Ilium only just now for you has fallen, for me it has fallen already, when the savage one (Achilles) drives his war chariot, my limbs had been dragged and the axle of Pelion (made from trees of Mt. Pelion, in Thessaly), trembling with Hector's heavy weight, was groaning with noise. Then [myself] having been overpowered and ruined, whatever has come to pass, I endure rigid and without emotion, being numbed by hardships. </i><br><br>While Helen just sits around and hopes for someone to save her, and when they don't she has to stip herself naked in front of Menelaus just to keep him from gutting her on the spot, Andromache takes her husband's death and stays <i> fierce. </i><br><br><i> Threaten with flames wounds and dire arts of evil grief and starvation and savage thirst and varied plagues from all directions and iron thrusted in my internal organs, the plague of a dark prison, and whatever the victor dares in anger. Courageous mother admits no fears. </i><br><br>And when they threatened to burn her husband's grave and throw his ashes over the ocean if she didn't tell them where Astyanax was, she refuses and tries to protect her son. Even when she's sold into prostitution she stays a staunch and proud woman throughout the rest of her life.<br><br> In fact, Andromache is a straight up badass. I wish a story would have been written about <i> her </i> and not Helen. I wouldn't want Angelini to write it, but I still want one written.<br><br>Honestly, now knowing what this whole story is about, I can't re-read this book without looking like a seizing cat:<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>'Nuff said. Er, shown. Whatever; you guys get my point. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10197872199866497597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7428328453028912774" style="display:none"><b><br><br>This is a story of an impossible love and two people destined to repeat history...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383821697i/6677096.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br>Wanna know who I loved most in the book?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383821697i/6677097.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br>I was never a fan of Helen and Paris, dunno why, and in this book the main couple certainly didn't change my mind.<br>I liked Hector the best, he is an amazing character and I wish HE was the main one instead of Paris, but oh well, can't have everything :(<br><br><br><br><br>The world building</b><br><br>Well, like I said, the main story here is the Trojan war about to repeat itself, and Paris+Helen's tragic love story happening all over again.<br>What's different here is that all the main characters are descendants of Greek gods.<br>They have special powers (when I say special powers I mean every damn possible power you can think of and then some you can't).<br>A bit too perfect for a half-god, didn't like that part.<br>There are pages and pages of rehashing Greek history (unfortunately for me, I know Greek history/mythology very well so I got bored at that part but oh well :D).<br>Still, it was interesting, it really was :DD<br><br><br><br><b>The story</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383823213i/6677614.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Helen is the most beautiful woman ever. And I mean Helen, a 16-17 (don't remember exactly but let's say teenager) girl who has known she was different for a long time.<br>When a new family moves into her town, and she meets one of them, Helen gets overcome with the need to KILL that dude from that new family.<br>Yes, it's hate at first sight, I love those and I loved it here too.<br>It all has an explanation, one I'm not about to give you (ehehehehe), and eventually, Helen and Lucas fall in looooooove &lt;3<br><br><br><br><b>What I loved here:</b><br><br><u>
  <b>Hector.</b>
</u><br>OMG! He is the best part of this book, I can't say enough how much I loved EVERY scene with that guy. EVERY!!!!<br>I would die of happiness if he was to get his own book &lt;3<br>But then knowing how wonderfully Hector's fate ends, I don't have high hopes :((((<br><br><b>The Greek mythology</b> and everything about it!<br>I love GM and I loved it here, though at times the explanations were a bit overwhelming and too detailed.<br>The whole concept of the book is great, different, and I really liked it.<br><br><br><br><b>What I didn't like here:<br><br>The main couple.</b><br>Let me explain:<br>I loved them in the first half of the book. Well, I loved Lucas *blushing*<br>All the love/hate thing was great and all, I have to admit.<br>But then, something happened near the end that really pissed me off, I was irritated and they all got on my nerves! All of them (except Hector of course &lt;3 &lt;3 &lt;3).<br><br><b>Helen.</b><br>As someone who carries the whole series, she never warmed up to me, I didn't like her at all. She's lucky she had Lucas as other MC cause I liked them as couple (in the first half).<br><br><b>The ending.</b><br>It was stupid and unnecessary, the drama that happened in the end. Well it happened about 85% I think.<br>It was so idiotic that I couldn't read anymore, I actually skimmed and read the last 15% in about 5 min.<br>I admit, I am not dying to read the sequel :(<br><br><br><br><br><br><b>Overall, the book was good at the beginning, great in the middle, but near the end I just couldn't stomach it :(<br>So I'm somewhere in the middle with my rating as well.<br><br>3 stars for Starcrossed</b><br><br><br></span>

<div id="review_92682702" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92682702" />
    <a title="Krys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2798856-krys"><img alt="Krys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329103793p2/2798856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92682702?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krys" href="/user/show/2798856-krys">Krys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=medium-length-book">medium-length-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=urban-dark-fantasy-paranormal">urban-dark-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=need-to-finish-did-not-finish">need-to-finish-did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=third-person-narrative">third-person-narrative</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92682702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11402505066831523524"><br/>I hate to say this but I am going to be tearing this one apart. I think I'm the first person to write a negative review for Starcrossed by Josephine Angelini on the entirety of the internet. But that said, here goes nothing.<br/><br/>This book did nothing for me. Nothing. Absolutely nothing. And here's why.<br/><br/>Starcrossed is set on Nantucket island and features the shy, willowy Helen as she gears up for the first day of her junior year of high school. She and her father live alone and she has a job and a best</span>
  <span id="freeText11402505066831523524" style="display:none"><br />I hate to say this but I am going to be tearing this one apart. I think I'm the first person to write a negative review for Starcrossed by Josephine Angelini on the entirety of the internet. But that said, here goes nothing.<br /><br />This book did nothing for me. Nothing. Absolutely nothing. And here's why.<br /><br />Starcrossed is set on Nantucket island and features the shy, willowy Helen as she gears up for the first day of her junior year of high school. She and her father live alone and she has a job and a best friend, but something is coming. Something that will change Helen forever. Before she can even realize it the island is abuzz with news of the Delos family moving to the island. Helen begins to develop feelings of rage and unrest as she hears more about them. She begins to see visions of three women demanding blood. And, worse of all, the minute she meets the gorgeous Lucas Delos she tries attacks him.<br /><br />Is Helen going insane? And what does all of it mean? And, why oh why, should I care?<br /><br />I heard about this book over a year ago... all the book world has been waiting for it. "It's Percy Jackson for high school girls! It's the new Twilight series!" Blah, blah, blather. I was as excited as everyone else, but I'm over it. This book did so little for me.<br /><br />Part of the problem is in the writing itself. This is a debut novel and it shows. Angelini's writing is less of a fluid storytelling style and more of a disjointed spewing of every thought Helen (or rather Angelini) has as she goes along. I watched as paragraphs of random thoughts congealed together to form what is supposed to be a narrative and I wondered why the character was so ADD. Then it hit me; Percy was ADD and this book is trying to be exactly that. I can't help but feel that Angelini decided to smash two popular things together to try to make something new and failed miserably.<br /><br />I see that she loves Meyers. It shows. The writing is so similar. The problem is that no matter how much I (and everyone) loved Twilight (and the subsequent books) upon the initial reading there seems to be a universally agreed upon fact. Meyers, for all her success, is not a good writer. She's great at character development and in capturing the essence of Bella's spirit but not a great writer. We follow Bella because we identify so hard with her. Helen is no Bella. She's drippy and annoying and easy to disconnect from. I found nothing engaging about her.<br /><br />To mimic something in tone, and do it worse than Meyers, is a crime. To try to tailor it after something that is so universally loved is also a bad move. It's going to get weighed against and slaughtered if it fails. I didn't even make it through one hundred pages and I was tossing this down in annoyance. I didn't like the voice of the main character, the smashed together plot line (which I feel I've read before) and the direction it was going. It felt overly contrived, and I was not amused by it. The only thing I enjoyed about it was the setting.<br /><br />I'm not even the hardest core Meyers fan and I feel bad for her. In this case imitation is not flattery. The formula is way too similar. I feel even worse for Rick Riordan who shares a very like idea. This is an example of how his books could have been done if they were done. Very. Badly.<br /><br />I wish I had more reviews up to compare it with. I know others are going to love this, and it will sell a ton. However, I did not love it. I did not like it. I couldn't go on, and that is always a bad sign.<br /><br />1 out of 5 stars.<br /><br />- review courtesy of <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bibliopunkkreads.com">www.bibliopunkkreads.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11402505066831523524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_433742147" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/433742147?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
