<div id="review_468553458" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468553458" />
    <a title="Merary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6508812-merary"><img alt="Merary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483176424p2/6508812.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/468553458?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merary" href="/user/show/6508812-merary">Merary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=stalkers-creep-me-out">stalkers-creep-me-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=the-worst-i-d-ever-read">the-worst-i-d-ever-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=why-the-hell-is-this-book-popular">why-the-hell-is-this-book-popular</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=you-are-an-idiot">you-are-an-idiot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=incest">incest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=left-me-with-a-passionate-fury">left-me-with-a-passionate-fury</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=boring-bland-main-characters">boring-bland-main-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=abusive-relationships">abusive-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=activate-insta-love">activate-insta-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer468553458&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer468553458" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer590055222644137842">You know what? No.<br/>Fuck no!<br/>I think rating it 1 star is being extremely generous in this case.<br/>What the hell was this?<br/>I was warned several times that this book wasn't good, but, like always, I don't listen.<br/>I guess I like torture <i>way</i> too much.<br/><br/>Oh, boy. Mother isn't going to be happy with that fact.<br/><br/>Do I even have to explain why this book was terrible?<br/>Yes?<br/>Well, I know I'm writing a review, but do I really have to--?<br/><b>YES!!</b><br/>Okay, fine. Let's get this shit started.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399518ra/773215.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Shit, that felt good.</i><br/><br/><b>PLOT:</b><br/>T-there was . . .</span>
  <span id="freeText590055222644137842" style="display:none">You know what? No.<br>Fuck no!<br>I think rating it 1 star is being extremely generous in this case.<br>What the hell was this?<br>I was warned several times that this book wasn't good, but, like always, I don't listen.<br>I guess I like torture <i>way</i> too much.<br><br>Oh, boy. Mother isn't going to be happy with that fact.<br><br>Do I even have to explain why this book was terrible?<br>Yes?<br>Well, I know I'm writing a review, but do I really have to--?<br><b>YES!!</b><br>Okay, fine. Let's get this shit started.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399518ra/773215.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Shit, that felt good.</i><br><br><b>PLOT:</b><br>T-there was . . . a plot? Are you fucking serious?!! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lupin: How did you know about Sirius and I? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Saying that this book has a plot is like saying that <i>The Last Airbender</i> wasn't bad!!<br>Here's what I got so far:<br><br>Helen lives in Nantucket. Nantucket is boring. She lives with her dad, Jerry. A new clan of <s>vampires</s> people arrived. Everyone loves them. Helen almost kills one of them. His name was Lucas. After trying to kill each other, they date each other. Helen wants to sex him up. He says no. Helen is upset. Helen discovers that the Delos's family are descended from Greek gods and Helen is one too. They go into training. Helen gets more powers. Shit happens. MORE shit happens. Lucas and Helen can't be together because the Houses have to be separated. Groan. More groan. Daphne, Helen's mother, reappears. Daphne tells them that they're first cousins. "You know what? This is gross. Incest, yuck!" <br><br>THE. FUCKING. END.<br><br>The whole story was predictable and dragged on way too long. This book is almost 500 pages long, people! And nothing ever happens in there!!<br>UUUUUUUUGGGGHHHHHH.<br>I saw the plot twists coming and I was never impressed.<br>Not. A. Bit.<br><br><b>WRITING:</b><br>Oh fuck, are you serious? The writing skills were amateurish at best! SHOW, DON'T TELL!! SHOOOWW, DAMMIT!! IT'S NOT SO HARD!! Basically, the sentences were too simple and its love for info-dumping was too extreme.<br>And let's not forget its attempt at similes and metaphors.<br>Oh, boy.<br><br>
  <i>but her insides felt gooey and soft, as if she were a freshly microwaved chocolate chip cookie.</i>
<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Helen ripped into the bread like a medieval glutton with low blood sugar.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>JUST LOOK AT THEM!!<br>And the dialogue? Trying too hard. What teenager says "What the holy grenade"? TELL ME!!<br>After several bad paragraphs (Which were a LOT), my head started to hurt and I was craving aspirins. ASPIRINS!! I HATE ASPIRINS!! And a drink. I'M UNDERAGE!!<br>Even my eyes wanted to bleed because the writing was too painful.<br>And did I mentioned the info-dumping? Angelini tried to stuffed all the Greek histories in short paragraphs, and guess what? I learned nothing.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399518ra/773216.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>If you want to expand some Greek knowledge, this is not the right book. Apparently you have to learn the ENTIRE story before reading this.<br>GAH.<br>But, this is nothing compared to--<br><br><b>THE CHARACTERS:</b><br>The main character is Helen Hamilton, the most beautiful girl in Nantucket. You know, kind of like Helen of Troy. Very subtle. Apparently, she's so SHY and AWKWARD and doesn't realize how beautiful she is. And she's clumsy. THAT'S SO ORIGINAL. And she's also a brainiac! Helen was made specifically to make the reader feel sympathy for her. Girls hate her because she's beautiful and every guy pays attention to her. The guys even call her <i>Heaven</i> Hamilton. No kidding. If you hate her, you're just jealous. And she has really super KEWL powers and gets stronger each chapter. She's the most powerful demi-god there was and nothing can kill her!! In other words, she's a Mary Sue. And an idiot. Oh, yes she is. And before she met Lucas, she's never have a boyfriend or been kissed. Because if she's not "pure", readers will think she's a whore that needs to die. Right. And even though she has super KEWL powers, she doesn't use them. You know why? "Because killing enemies is so mean". She is so damn useless. Why give her superpowers if she's not going to use them? She lets other people save her ass! I. DON'T. GET. IT. Useless, useless, useless! She is the definitely the worst YA heroine I've ever encountered. Sorry Bella Swan. <br>And she's part of a prophecy where she will save the world. Yikes. <br><br>Next we have Lucas Delos. He is so hot and every girl falls for him. <i>Because he is so hot.</i> And he has swimming-pool blue eyes. That's so creative. When he first met Helen, he wanted to kill her. And then they fall in love with each other. They can't live without each other! Co-Dependency for the win!! I didn't like him. At all. He orders Helen around (Even the quotations are marked as "he ordered") and gets horribly jealous when she talks to other people.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Is Zach after you?" Lucas asked with wide eyes.<br>"Oh, not really. He wants to talk to me about something, I think," Helen said as if it wasn't important. She shut her mouth before she could say too much.<br>"Yeah, I'll bet," Lucas said with a sneer, his blue eyes turning nearly black as he sensed her untruth. Is there any reason for Zach to think that you might be single?" "Are you trying to make me jealous or are you just so frustrated that you're already looking for someone else? Someone who would give in to you?"</i>
</blockquote><br><br>And this is before they were dating!! Basically, Lucas kept saying no to Helen, but is is suddenly a tragedy if Helen wants to be with somebody else. FUCK THAT. WHY THE FUCK DO YOU CARE??!<br>And he threatened to rape her at one point. Only because she wore a certain type of pajama.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I only have so much willpower, Helen. And since you apparently sleep in the most ridiculously transparent tank top I've ever seen, I'm going to have to ask you to get under the covers before I do something stupid."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Translation: "If I force myself in you it will be your fault because you tempted me with your transparent nightgown."<br>This behavior is not okay. Being in a relationship is supposed to feel safe. When your boyfriend is threatening to rape you, you BREAK UP WITH HIM. What will happen then when you're completely alone? Hmm? Nobody deserves to feel used in a relationship.<br>And he likes to panic Helen on purpose! Look!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"You're pretty cute when you panic," he said with a huge smile.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Because it is so cute when guys make you fear for your life for their enjoyment.<br>In other words, Lucas attitude toward Helen is like this:<br>"I know we can't be together, but I'm still going to order you around. Now go to sleep, you inexperienced woman."<br>I can't. <br>And if Helen dares to lose her virginity to another guy, Lucas will kill that guy!<br>Ah, true love.<br>Oh, and here's the kicker: <i>He watches Helen sleep.</i><br>Can writers please get it through their heads that stalking isn't romantic? Look, just because <i>Twilight</i> did it, it doesn't mean that people will find that attractive. And if they do, they have serious problems. Is this the guy women really want? An arrogant, creepy, abusive love interest with the excuse of having good looks? <br>*checks the best-selling list* But of course they do.<br>And apparently he switches places with Hector to watch her.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399518ra/773217.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>GAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAH!!!!!<br><br>The Delos family: Let's just say that they're kind of like the Cullen clan.<br><br>Minor characters: Claire, Helen's best friend, who always tries to prove that she is right so <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she <i>pushed</i> and <i>stabbed</i> Helen just to see if she had powers. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>; Matt, Helen's other best friend; Zach, guy that suspects that Helen is hiding something; and Gretchen, the girl that ruined Helen's reputation because she accidentally pushed the bathroom door while she was in it by accident. And she still hasn't get over it after 7 years.<br><br>We have the most fascinating and complex characters in the history of literature right here!<br>Sigh.<br><br><b>VILLAINS:</b><br>Just pathetic. We have Creon who pretty does nothing until the end. He spends the majority of the novel staying in Spain, longing for Helen. That's right. He lusts after Helen, too. That's not cliched at all!<br>And he says crap like:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>A lady never cheapened herself by using foul language</i>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>He had sworn to <b>remove the feminine evil from the cestus from the world</b> so that <b>all men, Scions and normals alike</b>, could <b>finally control their lust.</b></i>
</blockquote><br><br>FUCK YOU, FUCK YOU, FUCK YOU, A THOUSAND TIMES FUCK YOU!!! How can people still have this primitive mindset about women? And a WOMAN wrote this! A WOMAN! How can we still think that women are to blame for men's actions? How can we still degrade women by the way the talk, dress, or act? This is disgusting and unacceptable. <br>I know the villain said that, but it is perfectly clear by the way it is written that this message is being preached.<br>I'll talk about the message later.<br>Then, we have Daphne Atreus, Helen's mother. Short story short, she abandoned Helen when she was a baby and cursed her. And then she suddenly appears in her life just to lie to her and Lucas that they're cousins.<br>How pathetic is that?<br>She was a really annoying villain and I wanted her to disappear.<br>Then, those two <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[kill Pandora <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and Hector <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>kills</i> Creon, making him an Outcast <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br>I hope Daphne gets her turn.<br><br><b>WHAT <i>STARCROSSED</i> <s>PREACHED</s> TAUGHT US (WARNING: I don't mean to offend anyone with this. I'm just mocking the book's message.):</b><br>Hey girls! Did you know that if two boys fight over you, it is all your fault and deserve to be hated if those two get in trouble? Silly girl, didn't you know that men are never responsible for their own actions? And if you try to fight back, you're wasting your time. You're a woman, you always want drama in your life. If you're beautiful, girls will hate you because us girls are jealous harpies that want all the attention to ourselves. <br>And you know what? Let's all make fun of domestic abuse!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399518i/773218.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ha ha, look at her! She obviously liked being beaten up! Can't you see how much she enjoyed it? You know what? Since it is so funny, let's all pretend to be in an abusive relationship to justify your bruises to your parents! That will be a very funny family reunion.<br><br><blockquote>I'll just tell him [Jerry] you abuse me," Helen said with a shrug.<br>"And I'll tell him you like it," he teased back. </blockquote><br><br>And you want to fight? *dope slap* Silly woman! Don't you realize that men do all the fighting and you're supposed to <i>stay in the kitchen?</i> If you want to fight, do it to stay in shape! You're supposed to be feminine and round! No men likes a strong woman!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Everything about Ariadne was so feminine and round and lovely that Helen simply couldn't imagine anyone hitting her. "Do you guys do this to each other often? The fighting, I mean." Ariadne was shaking her head before Helen had even finished talking. "No. We spar together to stay in shape, but only the boys really fight, and only when they need to get something off their chests."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Your boyfriend orders you around? He's doing it for your own good and he loves you! That means he really cares about you! Don't worry if he tries to rape you. He's your boyfriend and you're suppose to do what he says! Besides, it's not rape if you like it.<br>And please don't curse! You're a lady, not a tomboy! Being watched while asleep is so romantic. Never questioned it. He's doing it for your own good. And if a guy rapes you, it is all your fault. Why can't you be more careful with your clothes? Look at your skirt! No wonder their penises couldn't contain themselves. *dope slap* Silly woman. <br>And oh my goodness! The guy you liked is <i>gay</i>? You know there's a solution for that, right? It's called getting a sex change.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>She decided that if Lucas was gay then she was going to have to get a sex change operation. He would be so worth it.</i>
</blockquote><br>You may live happily ever after.<br>And EW! You're trying to have a life outside your relationship? Why do you hate him so much? You're supposed to depend on your boyfriend! That's real love, you silly woman! You're not supposed to have a mind of your own, your boyfriend IS your mind.<br>And OMG what are you doing? Are you trying to have sex? BOO! YOU WHORE! You're supposed to lose your virginity to your husband and no one else. Wait, you love that guy? Screw you, silly woman! You deserved to be left behind when he's done with you! Don't you realize that men don't want a woman who has been deflowered? That's right, ladies. Your virginity is all you have. Without it, you're a big whore who deserves to die a painful death.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This book ends up being about Helen's virginity. What a surprise. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>In other words, FUCK THIS BOOK!!!!!<br><br><b>PLOT TWIST:</b><br>It's all a lie. Helen and Lucas believe that they're cousins and they suddenly stop loving each other. Huh. I guess the thrill is gone. It is legal to marry your cousin in some states. Problem solved! Oh yeah, I forgot. Fucking your cousin is disgusting. The stupid thing is, they're not related at all! This conflict is utterly useless.<br>UUUUUGH.<br><br><b>ANY POSITIVE QUALITIES?</b><br>Hector. That is all.<br><br>I could go and on, but enough is enough. This book blows. It's shit. Crap. Garbage. IT FREAKING SUCKS. Nothing more than a preachy, sexist book.<br>And it has a sequel! Oh boy, what did I do?<br>*sighs* I have to continue.<br>I think I'm going to throw up.<br><br><br><b>BONUS TIME!!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399518i/773219.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399518i/773220.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399518i/773221._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399518i/773222._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399518i/773223._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144302217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1314005165723519029">Very very good. I was unsure when I started it, having received a proof to read before publication, but a few chapters in and I was hooked! <br/>Angelini's use of Greek mythology adds a new spin to the relatively saturated 'Supernatural Romance' Genre that has suddenly exploded in teenage fiction. Helen and Lucas' cursed love story is touching and worth the read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_93125180" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93125180" />
    <a title="Vi Vi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2876847-vi-vi"><img alt="Vi Vi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302714242p2/2876847.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93125180?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

          marked it as to-read

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93125180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11205982437506225219">I'm getting this out of the library first, because I'm iffy about it. It seems like it could be interesting or just more angsty teen romance fair which I've honestly had enough of. But I'm holding out because it involves the Trojan War. Please dear god Josephine, don't do to greek mythology what Stephenie Meyer did to vampires. <br/><br/>I love Homer, so if this is just the Hot Topic/CW Network/Gossip Girl/Twilight version of the Iliad, I will honestly slit my stuffed animal's throat.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review576267403">

<div id="review_2396369666" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2396369666" />
    <a title="Caylynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66237296-caylynn"><img alt="Caylynn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594527171p2/66237296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2396369666?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caylynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caylynn" href="/user/show/66237296-caylynn">Caylynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66237296-caylynn?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66237296-caylynn?shelf=personal-favorites">personal-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2396369666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4976436558201478733"><i>
  <b>Reread #3. 4.25/5 stars</b>
</i><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“So, what can't you take? Decide which of the two options is harder, and do the other. That way, no matter how hard your choice turns out to be, at least you can find comfort in knowing you're avoiding something even worse.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>It's funny how, every time I reread this trilogy, I'm hit with just how far out of my usual genres of preference it is. Romance heavy, with starcrossed lovers and high school drama. But if you pair that with Greek heroes and reincarnation and c</span>
  <span id="freeText4976436558201478733" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Reread #3. 4.25/5 stars</b>
</i><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“So, what can't you take? Decide which of the two options is harder, and do the other. That way, no matter how hard your choice turns out to be, at least you can find comfort in knowing you're avoiding something even worse.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />It's funny how, every time I reread this trilogy, I'm hit with just how far out of my usual genres of preference it is. Romance heavy, with starcrossed lovers and high school drama. But if you pair that with Greek heroes and reincarnation and centuries of manic bloodlust feuds that stem from the participants of the Trojan war? Hell yeah, I'm going to give this book a go.<br /><br />Starcrossed is about a girl named Helen. She lives a normal life of avoiding drawing attention to herself and just trying to suffer through two more years of high school on Nantucket island. It's junior year, and enter the Delos family. A massive group of brothers and sisters and cousins from Spain who quickly insert themselves into Helen's school and intrude upon her life. She tries to stay away from them, given their status and her dislike of being the center of attention, but the second she sees Lucas Delos for the first time in the hallway, everything changes. <br /><br />All she wants is to <i>murder</i> him.<br /><br />She's instantly drawn into a hidden world of Greek demigods, reenacting an age old play, and the discovery that she's the modern Face that Launched a Thousand Ships. <br /><br />I really don't know how, but I fucking love this book. I first read it in 2014 when I borrowed it from the mini library in my teacher's room, and I was obsessed for the longest time. Thanks to Percy Jackson, I've always been in love with anything Greek/Roman wise, and this was definitely no exception. <br /><br />The characters are all their own individuals, and it's easy to keep them apart in your mind, even though there are <i>a lot</i>. Not only are the main characters-Lucas and Helen- carved out with unique personalities that readers can relate to, but a majority of the side characters are <i>very</i> fun to read about. From Hector's deadpan humor and pushy attitude to train Helen to keep herself alive, to Ariadne's feminine willpower and her connection to her twin Jason, to Claire's ferocity tucked neatly into a 5'2" frame, it's hard not to find at least a <i>few</i> characters to love in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9462795.Starcrossed__Starcrossed___1_" title="Starcrossed (Starcrossed, #1) by Josephine Angelini" rel="nofollow noopener">Starcrossed</a>.<br /><br />I absolutely recommend giving this book a try. It quickly became an unexpected favorite of mine, and I can still see myself reading it again and again for years to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4976436558201478733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5933971-sam?shelf=obsessed">obsessed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5933971-sam?shelf=brilliant-series">brilliant-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5933971-sam?shelf=amazing-loved-it">amazing-loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5933971-sam?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5933971-sam?shelf=book-with-gorgeous-boy">book-with-gorgeous-boy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5933971-sam?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5933971-sam?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5933971-sam?shelf=demigods-and-super-powers">demigods-and-super-powers</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192909577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16813167014284202275">Read more of my reviews at <a href='http://bookcrazedreviews.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falling Books!</a> <br/><br/><i>Starcrossed</i> is a book full of fun and action. It's an emotional rollercoaster. It will make you laugh, smile, cry and all the other complicated emotions that I can't explain. Josephine Angelini has created an exciting and dangerous world full of demigods and forbidden love that you can't get enough of.<br/><br/>Are you tired of reading about Vampires, Wolves, Fairies, Witches and Angels? Then <i>Starcrossed</i> is for you! If you think you know all the paranormal beings </span>
  <span id="freeText16813167014284202275" style="display:none">Read more of my reviews at <a href="http://bookcrazedreviews.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Books!</a> <br /><br /><i>Starcrossed</i> is a book full of fun and action. It's an emotional rollercoaster. It will make you laugh, smile, cry and all the other complicated emotions that I can't explain. Josephine Angelini has created an exciting and dangerous world full of demigods and forbidden love that you can't get enough of.<br /><br />Are you tired of reading about Vampires, Wolves, Fairies, Witches and Angels? Then <i>Starcrossed</i> is for you! If you think you know all the paranormal beings out there then you are wrong! I can promise you that there is no other Demigod book that could satisfy you more that this one. You will fall in love with all the characters in minutes after being introuduced to them. You will become addicted to the world where the sky is the limit when it comes down to unusual powers. Not once will you think, "This is boring." <i>Starcrossed</i> will keep you hooked until the very last word. <br /><br />Our main character, Helen, is a beautiful young girl who lives with her dad on a tiny island called Nantucket. She is a perfectly ordinary girl, at least she thinks she is. Until the gorgeous Delos family turn up. Helen is drawn to Lucas Delos, but has a terrifying urge to kill aswell. When she first sets eyes on him in her school hall, she thinks he is the hottest boy she has ever seen, but there's nothing like getting a little killing out the way first. Soon, Helen is sucked into the world of Demigods and mysterious powers that have been with her all her life. Helen's attraction to Lucas is becoming more and more visible to everyone, and too soon, they fall in love. But it isn't allowed. For Lucas is in the House of Thebes and Helen is not, if they are together....The gods will fall and declare war on them all.<br /><br />Sounds pretty amazing right? I know some of you are thinking, <i>"Demigods? House of Thebes? What are you talking about, Sam?"</i> Yes, yes, I know you want to know more, and I want to tell you. It's just that I want you all to experience the shocks with out me spoiling it for you. So, before I blab too much, <b>GO AND BUY <i>STARCROSSED</i>!</b> It's available in most countries.<br /><br />Overall, <i>Starcrossed</i> is a book that everyone should read and experience. I recommend it to everyone who loves a good complicated romance and greek mythology. Josephine will leave you breathless with this stunning debut that has touched thousands across the world.</span>

<div id="review_155144125" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155144125" />
    <a title="Lamia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4804393-lamia"><img alt="Lamia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294943987p2/4804393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155144125?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lamia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lamia" href="/user/show/4804393-lamia">Lamia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155144125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9092430579871651210">This can also be seen at <u>
  <a href='http://the-book-eater.blogspot.com/2011/03/review-starcrossed-by-josephine.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Eater</a>
</u><br/><br/>Actual rating: 2.5 stars<br/><br/>I was so very excited to read this. I basically pounced on the galley as soon as it was available.<br/><br/>I'm going to preface this by saying that this review is subjective. I think a lot of people will like this book. It just... Wasn't for me.<br/><br/>Throughout the whole thing, I kept finding similarities to Twilight. Helen, the narrator, is shy and extremely introverted - like Bella. She's gorgeous, but doesn't suspect a thing - like Bella. Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText9092430579871651210" style="display:none">This can also be seen at <u>
  <a href="http://the-book-eater.blogspot.com/2011/03/review-starcrossed-by-josephine.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Eater</a>
</u><br /><br />Actual rating: 2.5 stars<br /><br />I was so very excited to read this. I basically pounced on the galley as soon as it was available.<br /><br />I'm going to preface this by saying that this review is subjective. I think a lot of people will like this book. It just... Wasn't for me.<br /><br />Throughout the whole thing, I kept finding similarities to Twilight. Helen, the narrator, is shy and extremely introverted - like Bella. She's gorgeous, but doesn't suspect a thing - like Bella. She has an absent parental figure and a dad who's basically only interested in sports - like Bella. She has a weak personality disguised in bravado - like Bella. The prose is cheesy at times (<i>"It felt like the most natural thing in the world" "She let out a breath she didn't realize she'd been holding"</i>) and the romance only partly makes sense. Can you... Sense a pattern?<br /><br />The writing felt clumsy (I think the author used the word "cunning" 3 times in 5 pages) and very deliberate at times. I would read something, a tiny detail, and it was written in such a way that I knew it would be a big part of the plot later. And I hate obvious fore-shadowing.<br /><br />I also felt like the author wanted Helen to come off as strong. And, well...<br /><br /><i>"Helen nodded submissively."<br />"His gaze had such a positive impact on her that she felt unbalanced as soon as his eyes abandoned her."</i><br /><br />It's a shame, because this novel had a lot of potential. I love the plot and really enjoyed the mythological aspect (quite an original take on the Trojan war and the gods in general) and would have loved to see it crafted with more subtlety and skills. The romance, although kind of out of the blue (I love watching relationships develop - I'm not a fan of instant attraction), had this kind of <i>je ne sais quoi</i> (again, like freaking Twilight) that made me keep going. I think if Helen and Lucas were less co-dependent, the whole thing would work a lot better.<br /><br />To sum it up, I think the series has a lot of possibility if the writing gets better. This book is a debut, so I haven't given up hope. I'll probably pick up the sequel whenever it comes out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9092430579871651210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1163228-colleen-houck?shelf=gods-goddesses">gods-goddesses</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer504360161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7645625440686795770">If you like Greek mythology then this book should be right up your alley. Helen is a great heroine and Lucas is pretty amazing as well. ;) The Fates creep me out. I can totally picture them too which doesn't help with the creep factor. I was really liking Castor as the bad guy so now I wonder what Josie has in store for the next book. Can someone be even worse than that? Shudder. My favorite part? The flying. You'll see.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('diAwXpkQrntDQrwk1x8kxhR74TuPPWTi8pDkKVjPLKQrd9HhSFzBwwxp4Rnl7Fms1ZkPH1mgIZEysArf617E9g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Cfpzzb2fVYHpUyvxJ57vhouG1UaC84Jz+tLtZXo2p/NUrZJybNM6OaZ4dswVbZLsSmQ7YlRuxwA68gOTyadPoQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7756538150519547148">Josephine Angelini is a Massachusetts native and the youngest of eight siblings. She graduated from New York University's Tisch School of the Arts in theater, with a focus on the classics. She now lives in Los Angeles with her husband and daughter.</span>
